# Operator — Roadmap

*Last updated: May 6, 2026 (session 204 — 1-hour-meeting endurance audit kicked off; closed long-deferred `llm.py` product call via design refinement; two more endurance items queued; Apple Dev cert still in flight from S198).*

> **Current status: Session 204 — 1-hour-meeting endurance audit + resolved deferred `llm.py` follow-up.** New audit axis (resource/time behavior in long meetings, distinct from the static-cleanup pre-launch audit). Produced a 20-row suspect catalog across five failure modes: unbounded growth (transcript dict, tool-loop scratchpad, seen-IDs, log files), time drift (poll loops, silence-gap, heartbeat watchdog), stale handles (CDP, MCP pipes, OAuth tokens), retries, and participant flapping. **Top finding RESOLVED in commit `6b20483`:** every LLM call was re-reading the entire JSONL meeting record from disk to compute a 40-message tail; over an hour-long meeting with captions enabled this grows to MBs and adds measurable per-turn latency. User surfaced the bigger insight that captions were being prompt-stuffed at all even though the transcript MCP server already exposes them on demand — architectural duplication that also crowded chat history out of the 40-slot context budget in active meetings. Chose option (b) "keep tail but chat-only" over total deletion (chat carries a UI continuity expectation captions don't — people reference ambient talk explicitly when they want it). Fix: dropped captions from `_tail_messages`, added a `deque(maxlen=200)` chat tail in `MeetingRecord` populated by `append()`, new `tail_chat(n)` method serves it without I/O. JSONL on disk + `tail()` for generic queries unchanged. 19/19 tests green. **This closes the long-deferred `pipeline/llm.py` product decision** (`docs/pre-launch-audit.md` line 161, carried since S201). Two other 🔴/🟡 endurance findings queued for follow-up: claude_cli `_stderr_buf` accumulating every subprocess stderr byte for the meeting (deque swap fix); `macos_adapter.is_connected()` only checks an internal flag rather than actual CDP/page health, so post-sleep / network-blip the bot enters "looks alive but isn't" zombie state. **`openai` + `anthropic` Python deps decision is independent** of the llm.py question and still open — turns on "is a second provider in v1 scope?", not on how chat history is plumbed. **Exact next step (session 205):** claude_cli stderr deque fix (~1 LOC), then triage remaining 🟡 endurance items (MCP pipe death, OAuth token mid-meeting expiry, Google session mid-meeting expiry, audio helper 1hr behavior). Or pivot to standalone workflow passes (install dry-run is the highest-leverage one — `docs/pre-launch-audit.md` Pass 1, the #1 launch-day failure mode) or close the S203 phantom-feature product calls.

> **Prior status: Session 198 — Phase 14.20.4 SHIPPED + system-audio diagnosis locked.** Phase 14.20.4 lands `pipeline/audio.py` (152 LOC simplified `AudioProcessor` from voice-preserved — mlx-whisper-base, VAD constants verbatim, 0.5s pre-pad), wires it into `AttachAdapter._start_audio_pipeline` (helper subprocess + reader thread + two utterance threads, `set_caption_callback` mirrors macos_adapter contract), and routes utterances directly to `MeetingRecord.append(speaker, text, kind="caption", ts)` bypassing `TranscriptFinalizer` (whisper output is already finalized; routing through TF would double-buffer + risk coalescing same-speaker utterances inside its 0.7s silence window). install.sh codesigns the Swift helper with stable identifier `com.operator.audio-capture` after swiftc. **Mic confirmed end-to-end:** `CAPTION [user] 'Next test!!!'` and `CAPTION [user] 'Test test'` fired in live smoke from Cursor's terminal — full pipeline (helper → reader thread → AudioProcessor → whisper → callback → MeetingRecord) works. **System audio (SCStream) deferred to 14.20.5.** Three sub-fixes also landed: (a) **empty-buffer counter bug** — `systemStats.callbacks` was incrementing AFTER `guard n > 0 else { return }`, so quiet system → 10s watchdog FATAL on a working stream; counter now top-of-function before any guard; (b) **Cursor responsibility-chain fix** — new `pipeline/_disclaimed_spawn.py` ctypes wrapper for `posix_spawn` + private API `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim(&attrs, 1)` makes the helper its own responsible process; from Cursor's terminal post-disclaim, audio actually flows; (c) **soft system-silent watchdog** — `[S]==0 cb at 10s` now logs WARN + helper continues (mic keeps flowing). Helper gained periodic stats (`stats t=2s [S]=N cb / NB [M]=N cb / NB`, every 2s through 12s) for time-series visibility. **`excludesCurrentProcessAudio`** flipped from `true` → `false` to match voice-preserved exactly. **Audio archaeology breakthrough:** voice-preserved's hard-won line in their docs — *"ScreenCaptureKit requires `.app` bundle on macOS — silently fails from plain Python script"* — explains everything. They wrapped the Python orchestrator in a `rumps`-based `.app` (`/Applications/Operator.app`); the Swift helper inherited a sane TCC chain. We're spawning from plain CLI Python in Cursor → SCStream silently denies. **Apple Developer Program enrolled mid-session** ($99/yr, 1-2 day approval window). Productized `.app` + Developer-ID + hardened-runtime + notarytool path documented at `docs/apple-dev-setup.md`. **Until launch:** while Apple Dev cert is in flight, working through carry-forwards: 14.19.9 (install.sh sendoff/welcome refresh), 14.19.10 (fresh-Mac ladder live-test), 14.19.11 (`mcp_client.py` ~700 LOC deletion), pre-launch audit (`docs/pre-launch-audit.md`), landing page (`docs/landing-page.md` + `public/`). When cert lands → 14.20.5: wrap helper as `.app`, sign + notarize, drop disclaim wrapper from productized path (keep as fallback), real-Meet smoke. **Files committed `d05c514` (pushed) covers wire-up.** **Files NOT yet committed (this end-of-session bundle):** Swift fixes + disclaim wrapper + install.sh codesign + apple-dev-setup doc + agent-context audio archaeology + the throwaway `tests/_helper_smoke_12s.py` debug harness.

> **Prior status: Session 197 — Phase 14.20.2 + 14.20.3 SHIPPED.** **14.20.2** lands `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift` (288 LOC) — single binary that captures system audio via ScreenCaptureKit + mic via AVAudioEngine in parallel, writes framed `[1B tag 'S'|'M'][4B BE u32 length][N bytes Float32 16kHz mono PCM]` chunks to stdout, with per-stream 10s no-callback watchdog and TCC preflight for both Screen Recording + Microphone. Single-binary chosen over two-process design despite DECISION.md's "two procs simpler to reason about" — single cdhash means user grants TCC once per service against one binary, not twice; framing adds ~~10 LOC. Compiled clean (`swiftc -O`, 88KB). **Smoke-test results:** mic stream flowed perfectly (105 callbacks, 670KB, RMS shows real signal during `say`); system stream got zero callbacks → watchdog fired at exactly 10s with the diagnostic message DECISION.md predicted. This is the empirical replay of the spike's day-one finding — same TCC silent-failure mode (preflight true, startCapture succeeds, callbacks never fire). The SCK code path is structurally identical to voice-preserved's production `audio_capture.swift`, so this is environmental (parent-app TCC propagation, fixed by Developer-ID code-signing at release time per memory). End-to-end SCK validation belongs in 14.20.5 post code-signing. > **Prior status: Session 196 — Phase 14.19.8 SHIPPED in one commit (`a30537a`).** The sterile templated `Run? tool: args\nOK?` card is gone. Inner-claude now authors the permission UX in the streaming reply path: reads narrate declaratively (`"Pulling your open Linear issues now."`) and auto-approve at the bridge; writes ask a question in the bot's voice (`"Want me to create the issue 'Vacuum my room' on Engineering?"`) and gate as before. Three reliability fixes layered on: (1) **recent-yes auto-approve** — when the user just said yes as the turn's input, the next gate auto-allows so a single approval doesn't get demanded twice (chat_runner tracks `_latest_user_msg` + `_approval_msg_ids_used`; 30s recency window); (2) **tiered bridge** — `auto_approve` lists `ToolSearch` + `Read/Grep/Glob/LS/WebSearch` + glob patterns `*__get_`*, `*__list_*`, `*__search_*`, `*__find_*`, `*__read_*`, `*__whoami` so reads never round-trip; (3) **YOLO override** — under `OPERATOR_YOLO=1` the WRITE tier flattens into the READ tier (declarative everything) and the bridge `auto_approve = ["*"]` belt-and-suspenders alongside `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. Voice rule explicitly defers to the agent's `system_prompt` persona (`"do NOT default to 'Want me to...'"`) so caveman/pirate bots speak in their own voice. **Stale comment from 14.19.2 corrected** — `--dangerously-skip-permissions` does NOT skip PreToolUse hooks (live-confirmed in S196: handler still fires under YOLO; the flag overrides denials but doesn't suppress the hook), now noted in `claude_cli._spawn`. > **Prior status: Session 192 — Phase 14.19.1/2/3 shipped + slip pivot to dedicated-Chrome-window architecture.** Six discrete decision points, ~~20 commits, slip ends working end-to-end as a "decide-before-joining" v1. The strategic call locked this session: **slip = "decide before joining"; mid-meeting handoff is impossible with CDP-attach.** Why: Chrome 121+ silently disables `--remote-debugging-port` against the user's logged-in default profile (Chromium issue 40066423, security mitigation against OAuth-token harvesting), unbypassable. Pivot: slip launches a separate Chrome window with its own profile dir at `~~/.operator/slip_profile/`. Sidesteps the restriction entirely. Trade-off accepted: if user is already in a meeting in main Chrome and wants claude, they must close that tab and rejoin via slip. **Cancelled mid-session:** Phase 14.19.3c.2-6 (Swift+ScreenCaptureKit+Whisper audio capture) — became moot once slip Chrome could be a separate (minimizable) window where DOM captions stop being magic-killing. > **Prior status: Session 175 — Zoom DOM inventory shipped end-to-end.** `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md` covers every architecturally-critical Zoom lifecycle state: launcher page (state 1), camera + mic permission modals (2a — two sequential ReactModal dialogs, "Continue without microphone and camera" is a `<span role="button">` not `<button>`), preview + name input (2b — `#input-for-name` is the only stable hook, no placeholder/aria/name attr; Join enabled via `button.preview-join-button:not(.zm-btn--disabled)`), in-meeting toolbar (4a — aria-label hooks throughout), chat panel (4b — chat input is `div.tiptap.ProseMirror[contenteditable]` not a textarea, per-message DOM has `data-userid` + `data-name` on `.chat-item__sender` and a UUID `data-id` on the row for dedup), More menu (4c — `react-bootstrap` dropdown, `a.dropdown-item[aria-label]`), Captions submenu + first-run language modal + caption rendering (4c.1–4c.3), participants count + roster (4d — count exposed in toolbar button aria-label, `[role="application"][aria-label="<Name> (Me|Host),computer audio <state>,video <state>"]`). > **Prior status: STRATEGIC PIVOT (session 164, post-test-1.2-hardening): two-track product architecture.** Apr 25 11:00 AM PST: user re-upped $5 in Anthropic API credits last night and was already out by morning. Console showed Apr 25 = $6.50 spend across three models: Sonnet 4.5 $2.87 (matches operator's Sonnet 4.5 outer LLM in the log), Sonnet 4.6 $2.77 + Haiku 4.5 $0.87 (unaccounted by our log). Single API key in console — same one operator uses. Diagnosis (definitive proof in `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl`): the inner `claude -p --worktree` subprocess spawned by `agents/engineer/claude_code.py` had `apiKeySource: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `model: claude-sonnet-4-6` — meaning every `delegate_to_claude_code` call was billing API rates, not consuming the user's Claude Max subscription. Leak path: `pipeline/mcp_client.py:593` spawns MCP server processes with `env={**os.environ, **self._srv_config["env"]}`, operator's process loaded `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` via `load_dotenv(~/.operator/.env)`, child inherits it, claude CLI prefers env-var over claude.ai login when present. A "handful of worktrees" easily produces $3–4 of inner-Claude-Code spend because each delegate is dozens of internal LLM calls (Sonnet 4.6 sub-agents + Haiku 4.5 fast paths). API rates aren't hiked relative to subscription; rather, **subscription is heavily subsidized for the heavy-Claude-Code persona** — Max plan bills flat per month and meters by messages-per-window, not tokens, so Anthropic absorbs marginal token cost. API bills per-token with no flat cap. Same task that's effectively free under Max costs $1–3 on API. **This realization triggered a fundamental product rethink: operator today forces every user into the API-key path even when they have a Claude Code subscription that would cover their use case for free.** **The decision: pivot to a two-track architecture.** Track A — **plug-and-play claude bot**: `operator run claude` is the zero-setup zero-config zero-API-key default. Inner LLM IS the user's Claude Code (`claude -p` subprocess, subscription-billed). Brings Claude Code into a Meet, no other configuration needed. Personality + ground_rules pass through as system-prompt augmentation so the bot has meeting-tone voice (warm, brief, no walls of text) instead of solo-CLI voice. Permission MCP wires inner-claude's tool-use confirmations through Meet chat so a non-TTY caller can still gate writes. **The "claude" name is reserved for track A only** — the setup wizard no longer offers it as a choosable preset. Track B — **custom agent framework**: existing operator orchestration stays. Wizard pivots to "build a custom bot" only — the user names it themselves, picks a provider (Anthropic API / OpenAI / local model), wires their own MCPs, sets personality/ground_rules. Power-user path with the configurability we've already built. Two paths, neither with billing surprises: track A is free for Max subscribers, track B is bring-your-own-keys. The README's "Claude Code in your Google Meet" hero pitch becomes literal for track A; track B becomes the secondary "build your own meeting agent" story. **Launch is on hold pending track A.** The user explicitly: "I don't need to stop the bleeding now. I've made up my mind and want to fully pivot to this new direction now regardless of launch." All Phase 14.5 / 14.8 / 16.x dependencies pause until Phase 14.12 (the pivot) is complete. **Exact next step: Phase 14.12.1 — Permission MCP spike (1 day).** Probe whether `claude -p` exposes a Permission MCP host capability that lets a non-TTY caller (operator) intercept and resolve tool-use confirmations via Meet chat. If yes → track A is buildable as designed. If no → fall back plan needed (probably `bypassPermissions` mode for a sandboxed worktree, with the bot scoped to read-only ops outside the sandbox).

> **Prior status: session 164 shipped six commits hardening the live-test UX from Test 1.2.** (`1413318`) confirmation-decline UX fix — `chat_runner._handle_confirmation` now sends an unambiguous `[TOOL NOT EXECUTED]`-prefixed synthetic tool_result when the user replies non-yes during a pending confirm, so the LLM stops hallucinating "running, waiting for results" on a tool that never actually fired. Also added TTFT + first_flush instrumentation to `anthropic.py:complete_streaming` TIMING line — paid for itself the same session by definitively pinning a 50.3s call as `ttft=48.3s` (Anthropic-side request-queue spike, not our code). (`d0ff5a7`) stream-json side-log + live worktree progress — switched the inner claude CLI from `--output-format json` to `--output-format stream-json --verbose`, `_run_claude` reads stdout line-by-line and appends events to `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl` (truncated per call), `chat_runner` spawns a tailer thread for `claude-code__delegate_to_claude_code` calls that posts real inner-tool_use events ("Reading config.py…", "Editing chat_runner.py…", "Running: pytest tests/test_x.py…") instead of cute placeholder verbs. Closes the demo gap where a 5-minute delegate looked like the bot was hung. (`20a6d58`) drop verb heartbeat infrastructure — deleted `pipeline/heartbeat_verbs.py` + `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_SECONDS`/`TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS` from config; `_execute_and_respond` collapsed to a `done_event.wait()` since stream-json covers claude-code progress and short MCPs (linear/github) are quick enough that placeholder pings added more noise than signal. Tests in `test_912_tool_timeout.py` rewritten to assert silent execution. (`b1b5058`) stuck-LLM watchdog with one-shot status ping — `LLM_STUCK_THRESHOLD_SECONDS=45` in config; watchdog Timer in `complete_streaming` posts `"Anthropic is taking longer than usual to respond — hang tight."` exactly once if no token has arrived by 45s. Cancel in try/finally so it doesn't fire stale on a failed call. Retry semantics deferred (would require chat-reader/dispatcher concurrency refactor; informational ping is the minimum viable). (`5af360c`) drop trailing newlines in stuck-LLM watchdog message — live retest caught a self-reply cascade: bot sent `"...hang tight.\n\n"`, Meet's DOM stripped trailing newlines on read-back, exact-text own-message dedup mismatched, bot reprocessed its own watchdog as a user prompt and the LLM looped on it. Trailing `\n\n` removed. (`1e7e3e1`) ID-based own-message dedup + stripped text-match fallback — the underlying brittleness was that `chat_runner._send` told the connector to send but never tracked the resulting `data-message-id`, so dedup relied on exact-text comparison that any DOM normalization could break. Connector contract updated: `send_chat` now returns the new `data-message-id` (macos_adapter snapshots existing IDs pre-send, polls every 50ms up to 1s for a new one to appear). ChatRunner adds the returned ID to `_seen_ids`, short-circuiting at the existing line-341 ID check. Text-match fallback hardened: `_own_messages` now stores `text.strip()`, comparison strips both sides — catches the linux-adapter (still returns None) path and the race window where the post-send DOM read times out. **Exact next step: re-run Test 1.2 (`migration-plan`) cleanly with the new dedup + stream-json + watchdog stack live; if it passes, move to Test 1.3 (`test-generation`), 1.4 (live coding delegation), Sessions 2 and 3, then Phase 15.10.5 (`operator worktrees` CLI — added this session as a deferred follow-up to ship before Phase 14.5 install.sh).** **Launch target: Apr 28–30 aspirational, May 1–2 acceptable.** MVP budget: ~5–7h remaining (session 164 burned ~2.5h on six commits + diagnosis of the cascade bug).

> **Prior status: session 163 shipped the headless bundled-Chromium pivot (`273b4b1`) + heartbeat fixed-cadence (`0d6f0e1`).** During Test 1.2 (`migration-plan` skill) the user instinctively quit Chrome to open a new browsing window — discovered macOS treats `Chrome.app` as a singleton: operator was launching the user's installed Chrome with `--user-data-dir` + `--headless=new`, but the `headless=False` Playwright flag won (so it ran *headed*), and the shared bundle ID meant the user's dock click + ⌘N got eaten by operator's process. Quitting Chrome killed the bot's tab silently and `chat_runner._send` blindly enqueued LLM paragraphs against a dead browser thread for ~70s with empty `queue.Empty` errors. Five self-contained probes in `debug/headless_meet_*.py` validated the pivot end-to-end against a real Meet URL with `heyoperator2026@gmail.com` invited: unauthed walls headless + headed equally (so the long-standing "Meet blocks headless" lore was actually "Meet blocks unauthed/uninvited"); auth + invite + headless → admitted normally; chat read (DOM observer), chat send (textarea fill + Enter), and caption observer (Shift+C + `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` + `__onCaption` bridge) all work in headless bundled Chromium. Live `operator run claude` against the patched code joined a fresh Meet in 9.2s (vs ~13s headed), captions enabled, intro posted, real chat exchange + `linear__list_issues` MCP tool call posted formatted output end-to-end. Heartbeat cadence flipped from exponential (8→16→32→60s) to fixed 30s — stretching gaps read as "the bot hung" once long enough; steady pings read as "still alive." `tests/test_912_tool_timeout.py` updated (`test_heartbeat_interval_backs_off → test_heartbeat_interval_is_fixed_cadence`); test_config_loader assertion bumped to 30. **Stale memory entry `project_meet_bot_detection.md`** is now wrong (Meet does NOT block headless when auth + invite present) — flag for next-session update. **Session-160 Chrome-runtime preflight code is now dead weight** — bundled Chromium ships with Playwright, no real-Chrome detection needed; safe to retire in a follow-up cleanup commit. **Exact next step: re-run Test 1.2 (`migration-plan`)** in `docs/live-skill-tests.md` against the new headless build (the original test 1.2 hung last session because of the Chrome-quit-mid-tool issue we just fixed), then 1.3 (`test-generation`), 1.4 (live coding delegation), Sessions 2 and 3, then Phase 14.11 wizard MCP copy tweak. **Launch target: Apr 28–30 aspirational, May 1–2 acceptable.** MVP budget: ~6–8h remaining (session 163 burned ~2h on diagnosis + 5-probe validation + production patch + cadence flip).

Root cause: `_ServerHandle.call_tool` had a hidden hardcoded `timeout=30` that silently undercut the bot's `tool_timeout_seconds: 600` config override; its `concurrent.futures.TimeoutError` stringifies to `""`, producing the empty-signature `Tool 'foo' failed:`  error line; meanwhile the asyncio task kept running and the subprocess finished the work, so the user saw both "failure" and a completed delivery. User rejected the initial two-stopwatches-with-margin proposal in favor of a single source of truth: the MCP layer owns the timeout, chat_runner only drives heartbeats. Implementation: `config.DEFAULT_TOOL_TIMEOUTS` map with ship-level defaults per MCP (claude-code 600, playwright 300, figma 90, github/salesforce 60, linear/sentry/slack/calendar/gmail/drive 30, notion 45); `_effective_timeout_for` walks override → default map → global fallback; `_ServerHandle.call_tool` now accepts a required `timeout`, cancels the task on expiry, and raises an informative `MCPToolError` that flows through the existing error signpost; `chat_runner._execute_and_respond` lost its deadline/`timed_out` branch entirely. Heartbeat became exponential (8s → 16s → 32s → 60s cap via new `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS`). Tests: `test_912_tool_timeout.py` rewritten to match the new contract (added `test_heartbeat_interval_backs_off` + `test_mcp_timeout_is_signposted_to_llm` + `test_mcp_timeout_fallback_when_llm_fails`), `test_mcp_client_units.py` gained `test_effective_timeout_precedence`. Real safety net for transient bursts; doesn't fix single-call prompts that exceed the user's per-minute tier (those need either tier upgrade or prompt trimming). All pass. **Incidental fix:** `tests/test_skills.py` was missing `OPERATOR_BOT` default — one-line addition unblocked 5 silently-dead pre-existing LLM/ChatRunner wiring tests. **Behavioral finding confirmed (LLMClient):** captions skip the first-contact hint and don't mark the speaker as greeted — ambient talk is not a direct greeting trigger. **MCPClient race carve-out deviation:** there is no reconnect path in current code, so "tool timeout racing with reconnect" has no target; orphan-cleanup is already covered by `test_mcp_shutdown.py` — revisit if reconnect is added post-launch. Commits `e37b1c9` (tests) + `a23099b` (doc updates). **Prior status: Schema + wizard redesign shipped (session 132) — four-layer customization frame (Tools → Playbooks → Ground Rules → Personality) with yaml split and 7-step wizard.** User flagged that the three central customization levers (system prompt, MCPs, skills) had overlapping properties and no internal terminology signalling how they build on each other. Mapped the ambiguity and locked a four-layer frame with wizard-facing labels: Tools (MCPs) → Playbooks (Skills) → Ground Rules → Personality. Implementation split `llm.system_prompt` into two top-level yaml blocks (`personality` + `ground_rules`), composed at load time as `personality\n\nground_rules` so rules land last and get LLM end-of-prompt weighting. Hard cut — all three bundled bots migrated in same commit, no backward-compat shim. Uniform split rule: voice/identity → personality, always-true constraints → ground_rules. Only the text differs across bots; designer's personality kept its opinion-forward register ("That spacing is cramped — bump it to 16px" is the register), engineer's ground rules preserved the full tool-routing + delegation blocks. Wizard grew 5 → 7 steps with instructional copy on each: step 2 "Tools (MCPs)", step 3 "Playbooks (Skills)", step 4 "Ground Rules", step 5 "Personality", step 6 API keys, step 7 atomic write. Steps 4+5 pop `$EDITOR` (via `VISUAL` then `EDITOR` then `vi` fallback) with two modes — edit-preset gets a two-path picker (inherit-with-cursor vs start-blank), from-scratch is always blank. Wizard pedagogical order is ground_rules → personality (opposite of concatenation order — more intuitive to author rules first, then voice). `agents/README.md` gained a new "Anatomy of a bot" section naming the four layers and explaining the compose order; field reference tables updated (removed `llm.system_prompt` row, added new top-level `personality`/`ground_rules` tables). `CLAUDE.md` config bullet list rewritten to match. Tests: `test_setup.py` fixtures cleaned (`system_prompt` removed from llm blocks), `_step5_write` → `_step7_write` renamed. Commit `1fdbc4e`. **Not yet live-tested.** Pick up with live-smoke (intro-on-join from 131 still unvalidated too), then `docs/test-plan.md` Component B (MeetingRecord), then pre-existing `test_912` failure, then 13.2 log cleanup → 15.6 → 14 → 15 → 16. Budget: ~~14h vs April 19 launch (day-of). **Prior status: Self-intro on join shipped (session 131) — discoverability fix, not a roadmap-phase item.** Strategic conversation surfaced a real product gap: a user joining a meeting with Operator has no idea what the bot can actually do, and no idea where to tweak/shape its behavior. Mapped the four steering surfaces (tools = capability, system prompt = identity/always-on, MCP hints = server-scoped framing, skills = playbooks) and concluded the abstraction is right — what's missing is *visibility*. User scoped a one-toggle solution: new `agent.intro_on_join: true` field (defaulted true on pm/designer/engineer); on join, the bot generates a 2-sentence self-intro via the LLM (using already-injected skills + MCP context, no message history) and posts it to chat. Implementation lives in three places: `config.py` reads the flag; `LLMClient.intro()` fires a single `provider.complete` call with a strict prompt (2 sentences, "I can…" framing, no tool/MCP terminology, no greeting filler — focuses on outcomes/use cases to inspire actual usage); `ChatRunner` runs generation in a background thread (`_generate_intro`) so the polling loop starts immediately, with the main loop owning the actual `send_chat` call to keep Playwright single-threaded. Messages that land during the ~2s generation window are persisted to the meeting record as normal but their LLM dispatch is deferred — buffered into `_pre_intro_buffer` and drained in order on the first iteration after `_intro_ready` fires. On generation failure: log + skip silently (per user — fake-success masks the real problem; if the LLM is broken the next message will surface it honestly). Reconnect re-intros (no per-meeting deduplication — explicit edge-case skip per user). Updated `docs/test-plan.md` Notes section so the next session's test inventory must include intro-on-join coverage in components A (config loader), C (LLMClient), and E (ChatRunner). **Not yet live-tested** — `operator try pm` is the cheapest sanity check (TerminalConnector skips the join wait so intro fires within ~2s of boot); real Meet test via `operator pm`. Pick up from: live-smoke the intro on a real Meet, then start walking the test plan at Component B (MeetingRecord) per the per-session protocol. Carried-over: `test_912::test_timeout_sends_failure_message` still broken from session 129 (pre-existing MagicMock issue). Budget: ~16h remaining vs April 19 launch (day-of). **Prior status: Phase 15.5.7 fully shipped — live-smoked end-to-end via`operator try engineer`(session 127, commit`2a7de34`).** Live smoke surfaced one tangential bug in` pipeline/chat_runner.py`unrelated to the delegate path itself: the harness's tool-confirmation prompt ("I'd like to run X. OK?") was being persisted to the meeting record as`kind="chat"`, then replayed back to the model on the next turn — the model started mimicking the pattern verbatim as plain text *before* raising its hand for a real` tool_call`. Two visible symptoms: (a) every confirmed tool call required the user to type "ok" twice (once to the model's parroted prompt, once to the harness's real one), (b) sometimes after the first "ok" the model just hallucinated a result instead of emitting the real` tool_call`— caught live when Engineer claimed`/tmp/test-delegate-2`contained`README.md`when it actually contained`f.txt`(a file from a different repo's earlier turn). Root cause:`_send()`had no way to distinguish harness plumbing from real conversation; both ended up in the same`kind="chat"`bucket that`pipeline/llm.py:155-157`'s` tail()`-replay reads from. Fix:` _send(text, kind="chat")`now takes an optional`kind`;` _request_confirmation()`passes`kind="confirmation"`; the inbound-message persistence in` _loop()`tags the user's reply with`"confirmation"`whenever`_pending_tool_call`is set. Confirmations stay in the JSONL audit trail but the LLM prompt-builder skips them (only`chat`and`caption`are replayed), so the model literally cannot see the pattern it was mimicking. Re-ran the smoke after the fix — single confirmation prompt per call, repo-2 listing returned ground truth, per-repo session isolation intact (three independent sandboxes coexist across`/tmp/test-delegate/.claude/worktrees/sorted-shimmying-shore`,` /tmp/test-delegate/.claude/worktrees/vivid-mapping-hoare`,` /tmp/test-delegate-2/.claude/worktrees/dynamic-inventing-owl`). 15.5.7 done. Pick up with **Phase 13 — log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m)** — 13.1 was flagged by the user at session 124 start as "actually incomplete" and the specific gap still hasn't been captured. Ask the user what remains under 13.1 before touching 13.2. Budget: ~19h vs April 19 launch. **Prior status: Phase 15.5.7 shipped in session 126 (commit` 23bf258`) — delegate multi-repo + per-repo continuity + land flow.** Live` operator try engineer`run at session start exposed three coupled regressions in the delegate path: (1) every call spawned a fresh`--worktree`so follow-ups couldn't see prior files and the LLM silently re-created state; (2) sandbox worktree paths were never surfaced, so Engineer reported "confirmed working" for files the user would never find in their working tree; (3) delegate was hard-pinned to whatever repo Operator launched from — effectively "only edit the Operator repo," which is the wrong default for almost every user. Fix rolled into one rewrite of`agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py`:` delegate_to_claude_code(task, repo_path)`where`repo_path`is required; module-level`_SESSIONS: dict[str, {session_id, worktree_path, base_sha}]`scoped by canonical repo path. First call per repo runs`claude -p --worktree`with`cwd=repo_path`, diffs` git worktree list --porcelain`before/after to recover the worktree, stores the session id from JSON output. Follow-ups run`claude -p --resume **`with`cwd=worktree_path`(the key insight from verification:`--resume`looks up sessions by project dir = cwd, and you MUST NOT pass`--worktree`on resume or it spawns a new sandbox). Falls back to fresh worktree if resume returns "No conversation found." New`land_worktree_changes(repo_path)`tool stages all changes in the worktree (Claude Code leaves new files untracked so a naive`git diff`misses them), diffs against`base_sha`captured at first call, and applies into the user's working tree — fails cleanly on divergence. Tool result footer carries`[workdir: ...]`+`[repo: ...]`; Engineer's system prompt + delegate hints teach the model to ask for` repo_path`on first delegation, reuse it for follow-ups, mention the workdir when reporting back, and offer to land after success. README gains "How delegation works" section. Spec doc at`docs/delegate_multi_repo_spec.md`. Verified in isolation on three` /tmp/`fixture repos — create/resume-read/land round-trip clean, two repos in parallel hold independent sessions, no cross-contamination. **Not yet live-smoked via`operator try engineer`— explicit 6-step test plan saved to`docs/handoff.md`for session 127 kickoff.** Pick up with that smoke, then Phase 13 log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m). Stack dump showed the Playwright greenlet event loop wedged on`kqueue.control(None, ...)`inside`sync_playwright.**exit`**→`playwright.stop()`→ greenlet`run_as_sync`— the Node driver's CDP socket is dead (Chrome self-exits in`--headless=new`after Leave click) but the greenlet is waiting for responses that never arrive. Removing the explicit`browser.close()`alone wasn't enough: the same wedge can happen in the context-manager exit. Fix landed in`connectors/macos_adapter.py`: new` _kill_playwright_drivers()`helper`pgrep -P **`s for` playwright/driver/node ... cli.js run-driver`child processes;`leave()`now does`_browser_thread.join(timeout=2)`→ if still alive, SIGKILL the driver directly → re-join 2s. Killing the driver unblocks the kqueue.select and lets the greenlet exit cleanly. Also fixed a secondary symptom: a stray`participant count changed 2 → 0`log appearing *after`*left meeting`— added`if self._stop_event.is_set(): break`guards in`ChatRunner._loop()`after`read_chat()`and`get_participant_count() `so a blocked call finishing during SIGINT handling doesn't slip through one more iteration. Verified live: 3 clean pm runs (happy path ~1s shutdown, no safety-net line) + one tool-call run that hit the wedge and recovered in 3.1s (`force-killed stuck Playwright driver pid=84330`→`left meeting`4ms later, no outer Safety net line, no stray participant-count log). **Prior status (session 115) — Phase 15.5.3 LIVE-VALIDATED end-to-end.** Auto-admit confirmed working:`operator pm`→ meet.new spins a fresh room → human knocks → tray-click admits →`participant count 1 → 2`. Two iterations to land it. **Iter 1:** added post-action "pill gone" verification; revealed that admission actually succeeded *but* Meet leaves the "Admit N guest" pill widget sticky in the DOM (visible, not hidden) even after the guest is admitted, so a "wait for pill to disappear" verifier loops forever and a keyboard-fallback path was logging false-positive "admitted" lines every 2s. **Iter 2 (the fix):** swapped verification from pill-disappearance to **participant-count delta** (poll` _do_get_participant_count`for up to 3s after click; success = count went up). Added a`(pill_text, participant_count)`cooldown so a stale pill silently skips re-attempts until either text or count changes. Result: clean log of`admit pill detected text='Admit 1 guest' count=1`→`admit_btn count=1 visible=True`→`admitted via tray click (verified — participant count 1 → 2)`and then silence — no spam. New diagnostic snapshot`debug/post_admit_success.{png,html}`saved on verified admission. Found three issues, fixed all three, retested clean. (1) `LLMClient` and the captions path were holding two different `MeetingRecord` instances because `__main__.py` constructed the LLM before the record existed and never wired them — every `@operator` call returned 400 `messages: at least one message is required` whenever captions were enabled. (2) Same-speaker continuations were persisted as "prior + new" because Meet keeps the prior caption text visible in the same speaker's region; ported the `_normalize_for_match` token-prefix idea from `voice-preserved/pipeline/captions.py` into a new `_strip_prior_prefix` helper that's tolerant of Meet's casing/punctuation rewrites between finalizes. All 12 tests passed (Test 5 skipped per doc; Test 3 config-driven proof skipped). Confirm flow + correction re-propose works (`save_issue` `demo` → MOJ-16; `foo`→`gloo` correction → MOJ-17). Tool-loop scratchpad never persists (zero `tool_use`/`tool_result` lines on disk). Alone-exit grace fired at 61s. Two minor non-blockers noted: one DOM-poll missed a bare `ok` confirmation (recovered on retry), and the LLM occasionally needs a nudge to surface non-addressed context. Closed the session by auditing `CLAUDE.md` against the post-11.3a codebase — fixed three stale sections (architecture overview missing `meeting_record.py`, data-flow describing pre-11.3a "rolling history", config block listing wrong fields under `agent`/`llm`/`connector`). **Session 97 (April 14)** — positioning session after competitive research surfaced [joinly](https://github.com/joinly-ai/joinly) as a near-peer (multi-platform, voice, MCP, BYOLLM, MIT, hosted cloud, shipped 6+ months ago). Response: lean into **"Claude Code in your Google Meet"** as the launch framing and **opinionated quickstart** as the implicit differentiator. Added new **Phase 15.5 (Opinionated Quickstart)** — agents gallery + minimal `operator setup` wizard + a second chat-native agent slot. `agents/` directory created with format `README.md`; `claude-code` is the canonical starter. `docs/mvp-bar.md` updated with sharpened 3-part differentiation and a new Launch Strategy section (hero framings, visual hooks, distribution ranking, gallery as distribution primitive). Session 96 shipped 11.3a — per-meeting JSONL at `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` as the single source of truth for chat history. Phase 11 remaining: 11.3b (captions, ~~3h), 11.4 (skill loading, ~2h), 11.5 (Claude Code skill import, ~2h), 11.7 (provider keys optional, ~15m). 11.6 absorbed into 11.3a. After Phase 11: Phase 12 validation, 13 polish, 14 package, 15 cross-platform testing, 15.5 opinionated quickstart (new), 16 launch. Fast-follow audit items remain opportunistic. Post-MVP: Hosted Operator (~~30-35h). Zero-telemetry intact.

## Phase 14.19: Bridge architecture cutover — slip/dial/deploy (~3 days) ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

*Strategic pivot, session 190. Cut the entire custom-bot-construction surface from v0.0.1. Operator stops being "a meeting-bot platform" (a category nobody currently shops for) and becomes "the way to bring the Claude you already trust into your Google Meet" (a category that maps to a real, immediate desire).*

### Why this pivot

The wizard, the agent presets (`pm`/`engineer`/`designer`), the `system_prompt` composition layer, the multi-agent dispatch — all of it asks users to evaluate **a bot Operator constructed**, before they've decided they trust AI presence in meetings at all. That's a backwards trust ladder. The bridge model inverts it: Operator becomes a *thin meeting-presence layer* over a tool the user already has and trusts (Claude Code). Trust transfers; we don't have to earn it from scratch.

This is also a massive code reduction. We delete the wizard, the edit command, the `OPERATOR_BOT` env-routing, the `agents/` directory, the entire `agent`/`llm`/`mcp_servers`/`skills`/`system_prompt` config schema, `.env` loading, `READ_TOOLS` allowlist, much of `config.py`. Conservatively half the codebase. Less to slop, less to support, less to test.

The custom-bot work isn't lost — it's deferred to its right product moment as **Operator Studio** (see Post-MVP). Ships when users have already trusted AI presence in meetings and *now* want to compose their own.

### The three-rung ladder (locked verbs)

**slip → dial → deploy.** Each rung escalates one variable while holding others constant:

- `**operator slip claude [meet-url]`** — Claude responds *as you*; no second account; no separate participant. Lowest stakes. CDP-attach to user's existing Chrome session. Replies surface through your identity with a marker (default: `🤖`  prefix, pending iteration — see step 14.19.6) so the room knows what's you and what's Claude. This is the entry rung; most users start here.
- `**operator dial claude [meet-url]*`* — Claude has its own identity; you and Claude join a *fresh* Meet together; no other participants. Private one-on-one with AI. Echoes the 1-800-Operator brand metaphor. Good for solo brainstorms, voice-style sessions, transcribed interviews with yourself. Requires `operator login claude` to have been run once.
- `**operator deploy claude <meet-url>*`* — Claude has its own identity; joins your existing meeting with real participants. Full commitment, full visibility. Used for note-taking, project management, real-time research while you focus on the people. Requires `operator login claude`.

`--yolo` flag available on all three: maps to spawning `claude` with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. Default is ask-mode (claude pauses per-tool; Operator surfaces the prompt in Meet chat; user types y/n in chat to forward back).

### v0.0.1 = claude only

Codex and Gemini are explicit fast-follows, not launch blockers. The Phase 14.18B codex parity work (already shipped) gets re-homed under v0.0.2 once the bridge architecture is stable. v0.0.1 ships one bridge done extremely well.

### Zero user-facing config files

No `.env`. No `config.yaml`. No user-editable settings of any kind. Everything is hardcoded code constants in `bridges/claude.py`. Persistent state files in `~/.operator/` are runtime state only (`auth_state.json`, `browser_profile/`, `history/`, `debug/`) — written by code, never human-edited.

If a user wants persistent `--yolo` behavior, the answer is a shell alias. Operator stays config-free.

### Steps

| ------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| 14.19.1       | **Create `bridges/claude.py`** with hardcoded constants: spawn cmd (`claude -p --output-format stream-json --include-partial-messages --resume? ...`), trigger phrase (`@claude`), default reply prefix, transcript-MCP wiring. ~50 LOC replacing the entire current `agents/claude/config.yaml` + per-agent config-loading machinery.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | ✅                                                                       | ~2h                                                                      |
| 14.19.2       | **Wire the three commands** in `__main__.py` — `slip`, `dial`, `deploy`. Each runs its own JIT preflight (claude binary check, `claude auth status`, Chrome present, plus `auth_state.json` for dial/deploy). All three accept `--yolo` which appends `--dangerously-skip-permissions` to the spawn cmd. `dial` keeps current "open `meet.new`" semantics; `deploy` is the renamed `dial <name> <url>` path; `slip` is new (CDP attach).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | ✅                                                                       | ~3h                                                                      |
| 14.19.3       | **Implement `slip` mode (CDP attach) — separate-profile model.** Original plan was to attach to the user's existing Chrome. **S192 finding:** Chrome 121+ silently disables `--remote-debugging-port` against the user's logged-in default profile (Chromium issue 40066423, security mitigation against OAuth-token harvesting via DevTools, unbypassable). Pivoted to launching a **dedicated Chrome window** under operator's own profile dir (`~/.operator/slip_profile/`) with the meeting URL — sidesteps the restriction entirely. UX consequence: slip is "decide BEFORE joining"; mid-meeting handoff into an already-active Meet tab is not technically possible with CDP-attach. Documented as accepted v1 constraint; mid-meeting attach would require a Chrome extension (Post-MVP). Landed shape: `connectors/attach_adapter.py` (~330 lines) launches via `open -na 'Google Chrome' --args --remote-debugging-port=9222 --user-data-dir=SLIP_PROFILE_DIR --remote-allow-origins=* <url>`, probes CDP for already-running slip Chrome (instant re-attach), silently evicts non-slip Chromes from port 9222 via SIGTERM, waits for user to click 'Join now' (indefinite poll on the 'Leave call' button — no timeout, lobby admission can take many minutes). On leave: detach CDP only; slip Chrome stays running so the meeting continues.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | ✅                                                                       | ~5h actual ~10h                                                          |
| 14.19.3-quiet | **Quiet mode for slip.** ChatRunner gains `quiet_mode` flag. When True (slip): no intro generated/sent, no "Hold for {agent}…" filler, 1-on-1 trigger bypass disabled (always require `@claude`). Dial/deploy default to False. Also fixed self-reply cascade: AttachAdapter.read_chat strips the reply_prefix (🤖 ) from observed messages so ChatRunner's text-match dedup against `_own_messages` matches. Without this fix, the bot's own prefixed messages got read back as new user input, triggering an infinite reply loop.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | ✅                                                                       | ~1h                                                                      |
| 14.19.4       | **Implement `operator login claude`** — single-purpose command, not a wizard. Opens Chrome via Playwright, navigates to accounts.google.com, persists `auth_state.json` after sign-in. Lifted from the existing wizard's step-2 auth code. Idempotent — running twice refreshes session. No name-your-bot, no trigger-phrase prompt, no system-prompt composition. Just the auth dance.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | ✅ S193 (`ac93e89`)                                                      | ~1.5h actual ~30m                                                        |

Prints checklist: claude binary present, claude logged in, Chrome installed, git installed, `auth_state.json` exists (notes "only needed for dial/deploy"). For each missing item, prints the exact fix command. No decisions, no creativity, no construction.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | ✅ S193 (`3c1dc52`)                                                      | ~1h actual ~45m                                                          |

Test in a real Meet, eye-check what reads cleanest at a glance. Hardcode the winner in `bridges/claude.py`. No user-facing config knob.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ✅ S193 (`82694ff`) — winner: hybrid `[🤖 Claude]` (brackets+emoji+name) | ~30m actual ~20m                                                         |

### Post-MVP — slip-related items deferred from S192

The slip pivot to the separate-profile model (14.19.3) closed the original CDP-attach-to-existing-Chrome path. These items would re-open it or expand slip's reach; sequenced as follow-ups, not v1 blockers.

- **First-run sign-in friction.** Fresh slip profile drops the user on Google's sign-in flow inside the slip Chrome window. They figure it out without help. A friendly preflight in `_run_slip` ("first time slipping — sign into the window that just opened, then come back") would smooth the corner. ~30m work.
- **Mid-meeting handoff.** `operator handoff <url>` command that detects user is already in the meeting on main Chrome, instructs them to close that tab, then launches slip. Doesn't bypass the "decide before joining" constraint but smooths the awkward "wait, switch windows" moment when the user changes their mind mid-meeting. ~30m work.
- **Default URL handler.** Register operator as the macOS default app for `meet.google.com` URLs via Info.plist URL scheme. Every Meet link auto-routes to slip, eliminating the pre-planning problem at the OS level. ~2-3h work + first-run hook to ask the user if they want to set it as default.
- **Browser extension.** The only path that delivers "claude joins my existing meeting tab on a whim" mid-meeting. Different distribution (Chrome Web Store), different permission model (extensions can DOM-access without `--remote-debugging-port`), ~1-2 weeks of focused work + content-script architecture + IPC daemon. Reserved for after v0.0.1 ships and we have signal on whether mid-meeting handoff is what users actually ask for.

**Phase total: ~~22h (~~3 days).**

### Decisions locked from S190 conversation

- **Verbs: `slip / dial / deploy`.** Considered and rejected: `merge` (git collision, doesn't carry try-feel), `channel` (too metaphysical), `patch` (more about connecting than blending), `tag` (wrestling sub implies tag-out), `pair` (too software-jargon). `slip` is the entry rung's right-feel; `dial` keeps the brand metaphor; `deploy` carries appropriate commitment-weight for the public-meeting rung.
- **Trigger phrase: `@claude` (hardcoded).** No per-bot configurability. Edge case (user's actual name is Claude) is acceptable collateral.
- `**--yolo` is the only permission flag.** Maps to claude's `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. No `--allowedTools`/`--disallowedTools` exposed in v0.0.1.
- **No persistent permission preference.** Shell alias if a user wants persistent yolo. Stays consistent with zero-config-file goal.
- **Reply prefix: pending iteration.** Three candidates (brackets / robot emoji / italics) get mocked side-by-side; user picks; hardcoded. Robot emoji is the leading default.
- `**operator login claude` is not a wizard** — single-purpose auth command. Renaming away from the `setup` namespace deliberately to avoid evoking the deleted wizard surface.
- **Operator delegates MCP auth + skill management entirely to claude.** Operator's only "is the world ready" check is "does claude itself work." The transitive correctness of claude's GitHub MCP / Linear MCP / etc. is claude's problem, surfaced to the user via `claude mcp list` if they want to investigate. Operator does not duplicate this surface.

### Carry-overs that survive the cutover

- **Phase 14.18 transcript MCP** stays in v0.0.1 — it's the bridge's killer add over "just run claude in your terminal next to a Meet window." Ships unchanged at `mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`. The `~/.operator/.current_meeting` marker file mechanism (Phase 14.18.B1/B2) becomes the canonical way the transcript server finds the active meeting in slip/dial/deploy modes.
- **Phase 14.17 `--resume` crash recovery** stays — implemented inside the bridge, transparent to the user.
- **Captions** stay enabled by default (the YAML toggle disappears, the captions-on default behavior in `connectors/macos_adapter.py` remains).
- `**READ_TOOLS` allowlist DELETED.** Permission policy fully delegated to claude. Two states only: ask-mode (claude prompts per-tool) or yolo-mode (claude skips). No hybrid.

### Done when

Three commands work end-to-end on a fresh Mac. Zero user-editable config files exist. The `agents/` directory is gone. The wizard is gone. `operator doctor` cleanly reports world-readiness. The README and `CLAUDE.md` describe a thin bridge product, not a bot platform.

---

## Phase 14.20: Slip caption capture — Swift + ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper (~2-3 days) ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

*Promoted from Post-MVP in S193. v0.0.1 promised caption parity across bots (Phase 14.18 framing). Slip currently has zero caption capture in AttachAdapter — `@claude what did the other person just say` returns nothing — which breaks that promise for the entry-rung command. Closing the gap is launch-gating.*

### Why Swift + ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper, not DOM captions

S192 considered DOM captions in slip Chrome (cheap, ~1-2h, reuses `captions_js.py`). Rejected: slip Chrome is the user's visible window, Meet's caption overlay would render on top of their meeting view. The "minimize the slip window" workaround is fragile UX — users will forget, captions will surprise them mid-call, and the magic of slip ("claude is just there, invisible") collapses. The Swift pipeline keeps slip Chrome clean — captions are derived from system audio + mic, never from Meet's UI.

Trade-off accepted: two macOS permissions (Screen Recording for system audio capture via ScreenCaptureKit, Microphone for the user's voice). Both are first-run prompts, both surface in `operator doctor` (Phase 14.19.5). Granola does the same; users tolerate it because the resulting transcript quality is materially better than DOM captions (no auto-correction garbage, full speaker separation, latency ~1s vs Meet's 3-5s).

### Sequence and parallelism

Independent of 14.19.4–11 — the audio pipeline doesn't touch any bridge code. Develop in parallel after 14.19.6 lands (so slip's reply-attribution UX is locked first), and **before 14.19.10** so the end-to-end ladder live-test exercises captions too. Final integration into the ladder live-test happens in 14.19.10.

### Carry-over from cancelled S192 scope

The cancelled "Phase 14.19.3c.2 through 14.19.3c.6" (audio capture + Whisper) had already framed the dual-stream merger + permissions story before being dropped for the CDP-attach pivot. Design notes survive in handoff S192 § "Dropped from S192's plan" and roadmap context. Spike artifacts at `debug/resume_spike/` are CDP-related (different domain, not audio); 14.20 starts a fresh spike directory.


| Step    | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Status                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Time           |
| ------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------- |
| 14.20.1 | **Spike: ScreenCaptureKit system-audio tap + Whisper streaming.** Validate latency budget on a real Meet — target <2s caption-to-meeting-record latency to compete with Meet's DOM captions. Compare `whisper.cpp` vs `mlx-whisper` (already a dependency on the voice-preserved branch) for streaming throughput on M-series Macs. Deliverable: a 30-line Swift script that prints transcribed system audio to stdout in real time, plus a decision doc on the STT engine. Spike artifacts in `debug/14_20_audio_spike/`. | ✅ S193 — see `debug/14_20_audio_spike/{spike_capture.swift,STT_COMPARISON.md,DECISION.md}`. Locked: mlx-whisper-base (110ms inference, 4× faster than whisper.cpp on M-series), latency budget ~1.7s e2e, two parallel pipelines for mic+system speaker attribution, Developer-ID code-signing is a day-one requirement (not polish — empirically confirmed via TCC silent-failure observed during runtime test).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ~4h actual ~6h |
| 14.20.2 | **Swift helper binary — dual-stream capture.** Single Swift binary that captures system audio (ScreenCaptureKit) + mic (AVFoundation) simultaneously, merges to a single mono PCM stream with speaker tags (`[mic]` vs `[system]`), and writes either to a Unix socket or stdout in a framed format AttachAdapter can read. Build target: `~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture`. Built via `swiftc` in `install.sh` on macOS (skipped on Linux — slip is mac-only anyway).                                              | ✅ S197 — `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift` (288 LOC). Single-binary chosen over two-proc (one cdhash → cleaner TCC UX). Framed stdout `[1B tag 'S'|'M'][4B BE u32 length][N bytes Float32]`. Per-stream 10s watchdog, TCC preflight both perms. Mic path validated end-to-end (AVAudioConverter 48kHz hw → 16kHz target). System path structurally identical to voice-preserved's prod binary; smoke-test triggered the predicted TCC silent-failure (parent-app cdhash propagation), confirming watchdog logic. Live SCK validation deferred to 14.20.5 post Developer-ID code-signing. install.sh build wiring rolled into 14.20.4.             | ~3h            |
| 14.20.3 | **macOS permission UX.** First-run prompts for Screen Recording + Microphone surface naturally via the Swift binary's first call (TCC dialogs). `operator doctor` (14.19.5) gains two checks: TCC status for both permissions via `tccutil`/`sqlite3` query against the TCC database, with exact "fix it" guidance ("System Settings → Privacy & Security → Screen Recording → enable for terminal/iTerm").                                                                                                                | ✅ S197 — `--probe` flag on the helper (read-only TCC report via `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` + `AVCaptureDevice.authorizationStatus(for: .audio)`, prints JSON to stdout, never prompts). `doctor.py` gains `_check_screen_recording` + `_check_microphone` (darwin-only) plus `_audio_helper()` locator preferring `~/.operator/bin/` with `src/_1_800_operator/swift/` fallback. Fix copy points at exact System Settings panes. TCC.db SIP-protection rules out direct sqlite3 query → in-process probe is the only supported path (DECISION.md §2). Smoke-tested both happy + missing-binary paths. Cosmetic: empty `fix:` lines suppressed in `run_doctor()`. | ~1h            |
| 14.20.4 | **Wire into AttachAdapter + MeetingRecord.** AttachAdapter spawns the Swift helper as a subprocess on `join()`; reads framed PCM-or-text output; pipes Whisper output into `MeetingRecord.append_caption()` using the same JSONL shape as `captions_js.py`. The transcript MCP (`mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`) reads the same record file → zero changes there. Slip captions appear in `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` indistinguishable from dial/deploy captions.                                               | ⬜                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ~3h            |
| 14.20.5 | **Live-test on a real Meet.** Run `operator slip claude <url>`, speak a distinctive phrase aloud, ask `@claude what did I just say`. Verify (a) caption captured within ~2s, (b) stored in MeetingRecord JSONL, (c) transcript MCP serves it back to claude correctly, (d) speaker attribution (mic vs system) preserved. Then: same battery against another participant on the call (system audio path).                                                                                                                  | ⬜                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | ~2h            |


**Phase total: ~~17h (~~2-3 days).**

### Done when

Slip captions match dial/deploy captions in latency and quality; both macOS permissions prompt cleanly on first run; `operator doctor` reports both as green; live-test on a real Meet shows `@claude what did the other person just say` returning a correct answer.
