## Phase 14.18: transcript tool API beef-up + codex captions parity (~1 day) ✅ shipped S188 (`3ed5ff2`)

**Why launch-blocking.** v1 ships two bots — claude and codex — and the user wants feature parity at launch. Today only the claude bot has caption awareness (via the bundled transcript MCP at `mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`); codex has the documented gap from S179 (R8). Bot parity is a launch promise.

**Two tightly-coupled deliverables in one phase, sequenced deliberately:**

### Part A — beef up the transcript tool first

The current `recall_transcript` tool API is genuinely thin for real-world long-meeting use:

- Only knobs are `minutes_back` and `last_n` — no keyword filter, no time-window-around-X, no by-speaker filter, no length cap.
- Returns the entire requested chunk as one string. A 90-minute steady-talking meeting can dump several hundred KB into the model's context.
- "What were we talking about *around* 30 minutes ago?" forces the model to pull from 30 minutes ago to NOW (not a window around minute 30).
- "What did Sarah say?" forces a full pull and mental filter.
- `last_n` counts caption *lines*, which inflates for chatty speakers and undercounts long pauses.

We're going to ship beefier shape before extending to codex, so codex inherits the better tool from day one rather than us shipping the thin one twice.

**Step A1 — scoping spike (loose inspiration: the GitHub MCP surface).** GitHub MCP solves a structurally similar problem ("model needs to navigate a large indexed corpus of text") and exposes a curated set of tools (`search_code`, `search_issues`, `get_file_contents`, `list_commits`, etc.) rather than one dump-everything endpoint. Skim its tool list at session start as a primer for what shape our transcript tool *could* take. Don't copy directly — our use case is meeting captions (much smaller corpus, narrower query needs), not arbitrary repo navigation. The exercise is "what's the curated set of 3–5 query verbs that covers 90% of real-meeting needs?"

**Step A2 — finalize the new tool surface in conversation with the user.** Candidate verbs to discuss: keyword/semantic search across captions, time-window-around-X (not just since-X), by-speaker filter, summary-of-window, list-speakers, get-N-around-line. Lock final shape together before any code lands.

**Step A3 — implement** in `src/_1_800_operator/mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`. Keep `recall_transcript` for back-compat (or rename to a clearer verb if we add one); add the new tool functions; add a length cap with pagination/truncation hint so a model never blows context unintentionally.

**Step A4 — test (unit + fixture).** Build a fixture transcript file representing a realistic 60–90 minute meeting (synthetic captions, multiple speakers, varied speech density). Unit tests exercise each new tool function against the fixture for happy paths + edge cases (empty windows, single-speaker, long monologues, special chars). Run via the existing standalone-script test pattern.

**Step A5 — live-test on a real Meet, claude bot.** Open a real 30+ minute meeting (or simulate by pre-loading the fixture into a meeting record and running operator dial against a fake-long meeting), exercise each new tool verb via chat ("@claude what was the action item Sarah mentioned around the 20 minute mark?"). Verify the model picks the right tool for each question shape.

### Part B — extend captions to codex via marker file

Once the new tool ships and works for claude, extend it to codex.

**Step B1 — add the marker file mechanism** at `~/.operator/.current_meeting`. Write the active meeting's record path to this file from `_wire_meeting_record`. Delete it from `connector.leave()` and the shutdown handler.

**Step B2 — modify `transcript_server.py`** to read the meeting path from the marker file on each tool call. Falls back to the existing `OPERATOR_MEETING_RECORD_PATH` env var if marker is missing, so claude's existing path keeps working unchanged.

**Step B3 — register the transcript MCP for codex** in `agents/codex/config.yaml`. Append three static `-c` flags to `mcp_servers.codex.args`:

```yaml
- mcp-server
- -c
- 'mcp_servers.transcript.command="python"'
- -c
- 'mcp_servers.transcript.args=["-m","_1_800_operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server"]'
```

No path interpolation needed — the marker file replaces it. (Codex 0.128.0 supports `-c key=value` overrides on `mcp-server` per S187 spike; the S179 finding that "mcp-server doesn't accept --mcp-config" is now obsolete.)

**Step B4 — drop the captions-disabled disclaimer** in the codex YAML's comment block + flip `transcript.captions_enabled: true` for the codex agent.

**Step B5 — live-test end-to-end** with `operator dial codex <meet-url>`. Speak something aloud; ask codex via chat about it; verify codex pulls captions through the new tool surface. Run the same query battery from Step A5 against codex to confirm parity.

**Done when:** both bots have feature parity on captions; the new tool surface handles the realistic long-meeting query shapes we identified in A2; live tests pass against a real Meet for both bots.

**S188 outcome:** Part A shipped as designed (3 new MCP verbs + 12 KB byte ceiling + 26 unit tests). Part B's plan changed mid-implementation when the spike found `codex mcp-server` 0.128.0 doesn't expose `-c`-registered child MCPs to its inner model. Pivoted: codex uses raw shell + marker file instead, framework prompt directs it to `cat`/`grep`/`jq` the JSONL on demand. Same outcome (caption parity), different mechanism per bot. Both bots verified 8/8 on a synthetic load matrix instead of live Meet (user request — testing was driven autonomously via `operator try` with stdin-piped query battery). Three pre-existing bugs killed along the way (see "Hard Won Knowledge" in agent-context.md).

---

## Phase 14.17: claude_cli `--resume` for crash recovery (~half-day) ✅ shipped S187 (`4a4035f`)

**Why.** When the `claude -p` subprocess dies mid-meeting today, `_restart_after_death` (`pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py:553`) re-spawns cold and feeds a synthesized opener built from `_turn_history` — but `_turn_history` only carries `(user_text, assistant_text)` pairs, dropping tool calls and tool results (S166 deferred carry-over). So if the subprocess crashed after claude opened files, edited Linear, etc., the resumed bot inherits a sanitized story without ground truth and may hallucinate or contradict prior actions.

`claude -p --resume <session-id>` rehydrates a fresh subprocess from claude's local session store on disk (`~/.claude/projects/<project>/<session-id>.jsonl`) with the full message history including tool use + tool results. We already capture `session_id` from the system-init event (logged at `_validate_init_event`, line 582) — just need to persist it and use it on restart.

**Note on scope:** `--resume` does NOT replace tail-replay on the `anthropic`/`openai` API providers — it's a `claude -p` flag, not an API feature. Steady-state turns on `claude_cli` already don't replay tail (the long-lived subprocess holds context in-memory). So this phase is exclusively about closing the crash-recovery fidelity gap on track A.

**Cross-meeting continuity is an explicit non-goal of this phase** — `--resume`-ing a prior meeting's session-id when the bot rejoins a follow-up meeting is mechanically possible but sits in tension with the "fresh meeting = fresh context" default, and `MeetingRecord` is slug-keyed (no natural cross-meeting state). Revisit post-MVP.

**Steps:**

1. **Spike (~30min): confirm `--resume` + stream-json compose.** Verify `claude -p --resume <id> --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json` works end-to-end. The engineer's delegate MCP (`agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py`) already uses `--resume` but in one-shot mode (`-p "<task>"`). If stream-json + resume compose, the swap is clean. If not, recovery becomes a two-step shape: one-shot `--resume` to reconstruct context, then re-init stream-json — uglier but still wins on fidelity vs. the synthesized-opener.
2. **Capture and persist session_id.** Add `self._session_id` to `ClaudeCLIProvider`; populate from the `payload["session_id"]` already extracted at line 582. Set on every successful spawn.
3. **Rewire `_restart_after_death`** to spawn with `["claude", "-p", "--resume", self._session_id, ...]` (or the two-step fallback if step 1 says so). Delete the `_build_synthesized_opener` codepath (lines ~513–550) and the `_turn_history: list[tuple[str, str]]` field + every `_turn_history.append(...)` site (lines 699 + 827, plus the wrap-around references near lines 683 + 805). Also delete the corresponding restart path that re-feeds the synthesized opener on streaming retries.
4. **Test (live): kill the subprocess mid-meeting after a tool call; verify the resumed subprocess answers correctly about the prior tool call.** Kill via `pkill -9 -f "claude -p"` or similar between turns. Ask "what did you just do?" — pre-fix answer goes vague, post-fix answer cites the actual tool result.
5. **Test (unit): subprocess crash → `--resume` invocation.** Mock the subprocess; assert the second spawn call uses `--resume <captured-id>` and that `_turn_history` is no longer touched.

**Done when:** mid-meeting crash recovery preserves tool-call fidelity end-to-end, the `_turn_history` + `_build_synthesized_opener` plumbing is gone, and a regression test pins the `--resume` invocation.

## Completed Phases

Phases 1–6 + Caption Refactor + MCP Integration (all ✅)

### Phase 1: Extract the Agent Pipeline ✅

Pulled all "brain" logic out of `app.py` into `pipeline/` with zero macOS-specific code.

### Phase 2: Define the Connector Interface ✅

Defined `MeetingConnector` abstract interface. Wrapped macOS logic as `MacOSAdapter`.

### Phase 3: Docker/Cloud Adapter ✅

Built headless Linux adapter in Docker. Verified end-to-end in live Google Meet.

### Phase 4: Reorient — Cloud Cleanup + Linux Local Adapter ✅

Moved cloud artifacts into `cloud/`. Adapted Docker adapter into `LinuxAdapter` for local Linux machines.

### Phase 5: Config System ✅

All hardcoded constants moved into `config.yaml` with `config.py` reader.

### Phase 6: Consolidate Entry Points ✅

Shared loop extracted into `pipeline/runner.py`. OS auto-detection via `python -m _1_800_operator`. Calendar poller replaced `calendar_join.py`.

### Caption Refactor ✅

Replaced ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper with Google Meet DOM caption scraping. Eliminates echo problem, privacy issues, and Whisper dependency on macOS.

### Phase 11 (original): MCP Integration ✅

MCP client connects to configured servers at startup, discovers tools. Tool-call loop in LLMClient handles tool_call → execute → result → re-prompt. Chat-specific LLM settings. Config schema for `mcp_servers`. Validated with Linear and GitHub MCP servers end-to-end in live Meet. GitHub MCP server upgraded from deprecated npm package to official Go binary (`github/github-mcp-server` v0.32.0).

### Phase 7: Performance Iteration ✅ (partial)

Audio quality, TTS 3-tier architecture, latency masking, STT accuracy (mlx-whisper), streaming classification, playback interrupt classification, latency docs. Deferred to voice phase: TTS error handling/retry, premature finalization at 0.7s silence threshold.

## Phase 8: Chat-First MVP (THE CURRENT FOCUS)

*The pivot. Ship a chat-based task delegation bot as v1. Voice layers on top later.*

**Why:** A real user (engineer at a remote company) wants to delegate tasks to the bot via Google Chat during meetings. Chat I/O is simpler than voice — no wake detection, no latency tuning, no TTS. Ship something, get feedback, expand from there.

**Scope:** Google Meet only. Mac + Linux (Playwright is cross-platform, so Linux support is essentially free for chat-based interaction). Zoom/Teams deferred until there's confirmed user demand — each platform requires its own DOM selectors, join flow, and auth story.

**Core reframe:** Voice and chat are interaction layers over a shared capability layer. The audio pipeline stays in the codebase untouched.


| Step  | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Status                  |
| ----- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------- |
| 8.0   | Clean the house — reorganize root, consolidate docs                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | ✅                       |
| 8.1   | Chat I/O proof of concept — bot reads and writes Google Chat messages during a live meeting (echo test, no LLM). Create `ChatRunner` alongside `AgentRunner` — same `LLMClient`, simpler I/O loop. No codebase reorg needed; existing connector/pipeline separation already fits. | ✅ echo test passing e2e |
| 8.2   | Wire up the brain — connect chat input to LLM, respond in chat                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | ✅                       |
| 8.2.1 | Chat hardening — history cap (configurable), wake phrase gating for multi-participant, sender field extraction from DOM                                                                                                                                                           | ✅                       |
| 8.2.2 | Meeting lifecycle — pre-join user gate, end-time auto-leave, stale meeting skip, Ctrl+C clean shutdown, alone-exit auto-leave (session 86: after others were present, drop count→1 for 60s triggers leave; chat path tested live, voice path mirrored untested)                   | ✅                       |
| 8.3   | Ship to friend — minimal setup, clear instructions, get it in his hands                                                                                                                                                                                                           | ✅                       |

## Phase 11: Multi-Model & Customization

*Break the OpenAI lock-in and deliver the "your AI, not a generic bot" half of the MVP positioning. Voice deferred — see Post-MVP.*


| Step  | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Status                                                            | Est. |

| 11.1  | Abstract LLM provider interface — swap between OpenAI and Anthropic without code changes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | ✅                                                                 | ~3h  |
| 11.2  | Anthropic API backend — Claude as alternative LLM provider                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | ✅                                                                 | ~3h  |
| 11.3a | Meeting record as single source of truth — every chat-panel message (addressed, non-addressed, Operator's own replies) appends to a per-meeting JSONL file at `~/.operator/history/<meeting_id>.jsonl`. `LLMClient.ask()` reads the tail of that file and replays it as context on each call; no parallel in-memory pair buffer competing with it. Absorbs what was 11.6 (persistence) — the file IS the record. Tool-call/tool-result state stays in a small in-memory scratchpad for the in-flight turn only. `history_turns` renamed to `history_messages`. Meta header line in the JSONL (`kind: meta`, url + slug + timestamp) makes each file self-describing. Config-driven first-contact greeting via `agent.first_contact_hint` with `{first_name}` placeholder. Degrade gracefully when captions aren't turned on in the meeting.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | ✅ live-validated session 101 (T1/T2/T6/T9 PASS in `fqx-xndc-odd`) | ~3h  |

Each entry is either a single skill folder (`<name>/SKILL.md`) or a parent dir scanned one level deep for `*/SKILL.md`. On startup, resolve paths, parse YAML frontmatter (`name`, `description`, optional `allowed-tools`). **Progressive disclosure:** inject only `name + description` into the system prompt as an available-skills list; register a synthetic `load_skill(name)` tool alongside MCP tools so the model can pull a skill body on demand. `allowed-tools` filtering: WARN on tools Operator can't honor (`Bash`/`Edit`/`Write`/`Read`), still load the skill so the model can decline. Missing path → WARN + skip (no crash). Malformed frontmatter → WARN + skip. Duplicate names → last-wins + WARN. Startup banner: `SKILLS: N/M loaded (<name> ✓, …)`. Pitched as "Claude Code in Google Meet." See `docs/agent-context.md`. | ✅ live-validated session 104 (T1–T9 all PASS in fresh Meet)       | ~3h  |

| 15.5.3  | Runtime architecture — roster is the source of truth, not an ambient root config. Positional CLI in `__main__.py`: `operator <name> [url]` (run that bot in that meeting), `operator setup` (wizard, see 15.5.5), `operator list` (print roster + one-liners), bare `operator` (usage + roster). `<name>` dispatch loads `roster/<name>/config.yaml` directly; delete the root `config.yaml`. `.env` stays at repo root, shared across bots. `operator <name>` with no URL auto-opens `meet.new`, captures the assigned slug, joins as that bot (absorbs old 15.5.4's `meet.new` deliverable — same surface). Ship `./operator` bash wrapper at repo root as a provisional launcher until product name is locked and curl installer lands (post-launch). Breaking change: every doc/test reference to `python __main__.py <url>` updates to `operator <name> <url>`. *Implemented session 113; partially live-validated session 114; auto-admit landed and live-validated session 115 — positional CLI + meet.new redirect + JSONL slug capture + tray-click admission of knockers all clean on `operator pm`. Bot runs in headless Chrome (joins as host of meet.new auto-created room); `webbrowser.open(url)` spawns a visible tab for the human on the same URL. Admission verified via participant-count delta (Meet leaves the "Admit N guest" pill sticky in the DOM after admission, so pill-disappearance is not a usable success signal — count delta is). Cooldown on (pill_text, count) prevents re-attempt spam against the stale widget. | 15.5.5  | `operator setup` wizard — creation + reconfigure flow. **Pre-step (session 118):** MCP `enabled: true/false` flag on every block in every bot's `config.yaml`; `config.py` filters `enabled: false` at load. Replaces commented-out power-up blocks with real parseable YAML so the wizard reads one data shape. pm is the from-scratch baseline. **Wizard (session 119):** `pipeline/setup.py` with five steps — (1) fighter-select with two modes (from-scratch clones pm baseline + prompts for name/display/trigger/tagline/user-display with collision re-prompt reserving `setup`/`list` and existing agents; preset inherits name and edits in place); (2) power-ups — numbered-list `[ ]`/`[✓]` toggle flipping each MCP's `enabled` flag (Rich swallows literal `[x]` as a markup tag — switched to `[✓]`); (3) skills — user-added paths (folder, parent of folders, or single `.md` wrapped in a stem folder as SKILL.md) + bundled skills from the base bot as same toggle pattern (default all-checked, copied into `agents/<name>/skills/`); (4) API keys — prompt for any `${VAR}` referenced by an enabled MCP that isn't already in `.env`, append-only; (5) atomic write via tempdir + `os.rename`. Edit-in-place **seeds the tempdir with the existing bundle** before overwriting owned files (config.yaml, portrait.txt), fully re-authors `skills/`, and only writes a README stub when absent — preserves `.env.example`, delegate scripts, and hand-written READMEs that the wizard doesn't own (fix landed after live smoke-test revealed wholesale-replacement wiping those files). `.bak-<timestamp>` swap is the abort-recovery path. `rich` added to `requirements.txt`. `tests/test_setup.py` — 10/10 green. Smoke-tested both modes end-to-end. Known tradeoff: YAML comments on config.yaml are lost (no ruamel dep); values semantically preserved. **Session 124:** added `description:` field to every `mcp_servers.<name>` block across engineer/pm/designer; wizard step 2 renders it as the sublabel under each MCP name so "delegate" (and future bundle-specific MCPs) no longer look opaque in the power-ups picker. Runtime ignores the field.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | ✅      | ~4h                                             |
| 15.5.6  | `operator try <name>` — local test-drive before joining a Meet. New `connectors/terminal.py` implementing `MeetingConnector` via stdin/stdout: `read_chat` pulls from a queue fed by a stdin reader thread (non-blocking poll, returns `[]` when empty), `send_chat` prints `[<bot-name>] <msg>` with a colored prefix, `get_participant_count` returns 2 (forces 1-on-1 mode — no `@operator` prefix needed), `is_connected` stays True, `set_caption_callback` no-ops, `join/leave` are no-ops. `/quit` and EOF route through `os.kill(pid, SIGINT)` so shutdown mirrors Ctrl+C and skips ChatRunner's "connection lost" warning. New CLI verb in `__main__.py`: `operator try <name>` sets `OPERATOR_BOT`, builds provider + MCP + skills like the normal path, prints the startup banner, instantiates `TerminalConnector`, runs the full `ChatRunner`. `try` added to `RESERVED_NAMES` in `pipeline/setup.py`. `agents/README.md` Using-an-agent block gained the `operator try` step. Live-validated session 125 end-to-end against engineer bundle — terminal harness booted, confirm gate fired, heartbeats streamed, delegate ran `claude -p --worktree` successfully once permission-mode was fixed (see Hard Won Knowledge). Harness surfaced three other bugs in the same session that would've taken 3× Meet roundtrips to find otherwise: (a) delegate `claude -p` needs `--permission-mode bypassPermissions` (was defaulting to ask-mode with no TTY → every Write/Bash denied); made configurable via `DELEGATE_PERMISSION_MODE` env in `agents/engineer/config.yaml`, (b) Engineer system-prompt routing gap — model reached for `github__get_file_contents` on local path questions and hit 404s; tightened with a "github__* is remote-only, local ops go through delegate" paragraph, (c) tool-failure UX — replaced hardcoded "Sorry, that tool call failed. Check the logs" with LLM-authored recovery via new `ChatRunner._handle_tool_failure` helper (signposts the error back through `send_tool_result` with a disposition instruction, then dispatches the LLM's response). Also added `TIMING llm_call=...s TOKENS in=N cache_read=N cache_create=N out=N cache_hit=P%` logging across `pipeline/providers/{anthropic,openai}.py` and split the `tool_exec` span from the 2nd-LLM span in `chat_runner.py`'s `_execute_and_respond` — confirmed prompt cache is hitting 95–98% across turns; per-turn latency ceiling is the delegate subprocess itself (10–15s for `claude -p` boot + tool loop), not Operator overhead.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | ✅      | ~1h (actual ~2h incl. harness-driven bug fixes) |
| 15.5.7  | Delegate multi-repo + per-repo continuity (+ session-127 live-smoke fix to confirmation persistence). Live smoke of `operator try engineer` in session 126 surfaced three coupled bugs in `agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py`: (a) every delegate call spawned a fresh `--worktree`, so "prove it" / "now add tests" couldn't see files from the previous call and the LLM silently recreated state; (b) sandbox worktrees lived under Operator's own `.claude/worktrees/` with no path surfaced to the user — Engineer reported "confirmed working" for files that never existed in the user's working tree; (c) the tool was hard-pinned to whatever repo Operator was launched from, which is almost never the repo the user wants to work in. Rewrite: `delegate_to_claude_code(task, repo_path)` where `repo_path` is a required absolute path to a local git repo; module-level `_SESSIONS` dict maps canonical `repo_path` → `{session_id, worktree_path, base_sha}`. First call per repo runs `claude -p <task> --worktree` with `cwd=repo_path`, captures the new entry from `git worktree list --porcelain` diff and stores `session_id` from the JSON output. Subsequent calls same repo run `claude -p <task> --resume <id>` with `cwd=worktree_path` (critical: `--resume` looks up the session by project dir = cwd, and does NOT accept `--worktree` — that would spawn a new sandbox). Fall back to a fresh worktree if resume returns "No conversation found" (sandbox manually deleted between calls). New `land_worktree_changes(repo_path)` tool runs `git add -A` in the worktree (Claude Code leaves new files untracked — diff would otherwise be empty), then `git diff --cached <base_sha>` → `git apply` into the parent repo. Fails cleanly (reports the conflict) if the user's tree has diverged. Tool result footer on every delegate now includes `[workdir: ...]` and `[repo: ...]` lines; Engineer's system prompt teaches it to ask for `repo_path` on first delegation, reuse it for follow-ups, mention the workdir when reporting back, and offer to land after success. README gains a "How delegation works" section. Spec doc at `docs/delegate_multi_repo_spec.md`. Verified in isolation against three fresh `/tmp/` git repos: create → resume-read → land round-trip clean; two repos in one process hold independent sessions with no cross-contamination. Commit `23bf258`. **Live-smoked end-to-end session 127** — full 8-step plan walked against fresh `/tmp/test-delegate` + `/tmp/test-delegate-2` scratch repos: ask-for-repo-on-first-call ✅, sandbox isolation ✅ (file lived under `.claude/worktrees/<name>/scratch/`, not in user's working tree), `--resume` reused same workdir on follow-ups ✅, multi-repo isolation ✅ (independent sandboxes per repo), `land_worktree_changes` correctly stages-and-applies new files into the user's working tree in 0.1s ✅. Live smoke also surfaced and fixed a separate `pipeline/chat_runner.py` bug (commit `2a7de34`): tool-confirmation messages were persisted with `kind="chat"` and the model started mimicking the harness's "I'd like to run X. OK?" prompt verbatim before raising its hand for a real tool_call — fix tags both the harness's prompt and the user's "ok"/"no" reply with `kind="confirmation"`, which `pipeline/llm.py` already filters out of the LLM prompt. See Hard Won Knowledge for the full diagnosis. | ✅      | ~3h                                             |


**Phase total: ~19.75h**

## Phase 15.6: Pre-Launch Security

*Second pre-launch security pass. Phase 9.5 covered general input sanitization, credential handling, and dependency hygiene; this phase targets live-meeting prompt injection into a write-capable tool loop. Motivated by the OpenClaw/ClawHub security-vulnerability backlash on a peer OSS project — being publicly audit-ready at launch matters for both liability and adoption flywheel. **Session 139 reshape:** original 15.6.2 (core-repo `agents/CONTRIBUTING.md` + CODEOWNERS contribution gate) moved to post-MVP after ClawHub case-study research (341/2857 marketplace skills malicious; top-downloaded entries were malware; primary attack vector was prompt injection embedded in skill markdown, not config). Core-repo contributions with a maintainer review gate is the wrong shape for a solo maintainer — pivoted to an external gallery model (users clone from a separate index repo into their own `agents/`; runtime skill-markdown delimiter wrapper is the one non-theater mitigation we'll owe). See Post-MVP → Community & Gallery. **Sequenced after 13 (session 105):** clean code is easier to audit, and any fixes land before packaging + cross-platform testing. **No third-party audit pre-launch** (wrong stage, wrong timeline) — OSS-native transparency substitutes: threat-model doc, disclosure channel, and a self-audit driven by the `security-review` skill. Live-smoke of sessions 131 + 132 + 136 + 137 moves to after this phase (audited code gets smoked, not pre-audit code).*


| Step   | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Status     | Est. |
| ------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------- | ---- |
| 15.6.1 | Runtime security review + public-facing security artifacts. **Step 0:** run the `security-review` skill on the diff since 9.5 to drive the mitigation inventory. **Named surfaces (severity-ranked):** (a) `delegate_to_claude_code` is the highest-severity write path — spawns `claude -p --permission-mode bypassPermissions` against a user-supplied `repo_path` with a user-supplied `task`, so the confirmation gate is the only thing between a chat message and arbitrary code execution in the user's repo. Verify the confirm UI renders full `task` + `repo_path` legibly; check obfuscated-payload cases. (b) MCP tool writes (Linear `save_issue`, GitHub writes) — direct injection via chat + indirect injection via poisoned tool-result strings feeding back into the next prompt. Does the confirmation flow hold under social engineering? Are tool-result strings sanitized before re-prompting? (c) Captions-as-prompt-injection vector — `captions_enabled: true` on pm + designer means anyone *speaking* in the meeting injects into the LLM prompt, bypassing the `@operator` trigger gate entirely. Document mitigation or explicit residual risk. (d) MCP server command validation — `config.yaml` declares `command` + `args` for subprocesses; ensure no shell-injection path, and that a contributed `agents/<name>/config.yaml` can't smuggle arbitrary binaries. (e) Log sanitation — grep `/tmp/operator.log` for leaked API keys, tokens, full `.env` dumps, OAuth cookies; redact as needed. (f) `browser_profile/` + `auth_state.json` threat-model note — these hold real Google session cookies; document the blast radius if any other surface lands code execution. **Deliverables:** (1) `SECURITY.md` at repo root with GitHub-recognized disclosure email + response-time expectation, (2) `docs/security.md` — user-facing threat model, mitigations, known residual risks, and token-scoping guidance (fine-grained GitHub PATs, narrow Linear/Figma scopes, scoped `.env`), (3) `pip-audit` run against the pinned requirements (coordinates with 14.2). **Session 137:** audit done, 6 behavioural fixes shipped (Fix #0 `auth_state.json` in `.gitignore`, Fix #1 delimiter wrappers + label sanitizers, Fix #2 tool-arg redaction, Fix #3 unsafe env-key strip, Fix #4 confirmation shows all args with head/tail truncation, Fix #5 path-hygiene + `browser_profile/` chmod 0o700) across 5 commits `8d29b23…d1fa9fa`. **Session 138:** `SECURITY.md` (disclosure contact + 72h ack SLA + GitHub recognition) + `docs/security.md` (threat model, trust boundaries, residual risks H1/H2/L1–L4, "never commit" canonical list, "what's been hardened" section citing each fix commit, `NODE_OPTIONS`/`RUBYOPT`/`PERL5LIB`/`CLASSPATH`/`HOME` noted as residual env-key candidates for non-Python MCP runtimes); `pip-audit` flagged 5 CVEs across 4 transitive deps (cryptography, pygments, python-multipart, requests), added `>=` security floors to `requirements.txt` (full pinning defers to 14.2), re-audit clean, smoke tests pass. | ✅          | ~5h  |
| 15.6.2 | ~~Contribution security gate — `agents/CONTRIBUTING.md` + CODEOWNERS.~~ **Moved to post-MVP (session 139)** after research into ClawHub (OpenClaw's public skill marketplace — closest OSS peer to what this row originally proposed). Findings: 341/2857 ClawHub skills malicious, 5 of top 7 most-downloaded were malware, attack vector was prompt-injection instructions embedded in `SKILL.md` directing the AI to walk the user through downloading external payloads. "Narrow the contribution surface to config + markdown only" doesn't help because markdown *is* the attack surface. Block-before-publish scanning + verified authors + kill switch are the non-theater mitigations, and they're a team-sized project, not a 1.5h row. Pivoted to a gallery model (separate index repo, caveat-emptor, user owns the trust decision — `npm install` / `brew tap` / Claude Desktop MCP precedent). See **Post-MVP → Community & Gallery**. **Phase total: ~5h** (15.6.1 shipped; 15.6.2 moved to post-MVP)

## Phase 14: Package & Distribution

*Expanded from "minimal packaging" (session 141) to a real install path. Ship a `curl | sh` one-liner that installs Operator via `uv tool install` from a git URL, with agents extracted to a user dir (`~/.operator/agents/`) so the shipped package is immutable. **Deliberately skipping PyPI for MVP** — `uv tool install git+https://github.com/.../operator.git` gives the same install ergonomics without PyPI account/metadata overhead; PyPI moves to post-MVP polish. **Sequenced after 15.6 (session 105):** package the audited code, not pre-audit code.*

| 14.10   | Wizard Google-signin step — Meet joining requires a logged-in Chrome profile; pre-14.10 the only way to populate it was to `operator run <bot>`, hit a blank Meet screen, and manually navigate to `accounts.google.com` inside the launched browser. Fast-path detect reads `~/.operator/auth_state.json` (re-uses `session.validate_auth_state`) + cached `~/.operator/google_account.json` (`{"email": "..."}`) — instant, shows `✓ signed in as <email>` with `[enter] continue / [r] sign in with a different account`. Re-auth path navigates to `accounts.google.com/Logout` then `ServiceLogin` inside the same persistent profile (no nuking the 1.1 GB `browser_profile/`). First-time path launches visible Chrome to `accounts.google.com`, polls cookie jar for `.google.com` SID, then captures the email from the live `myaccount.google.com` DOM (free — page is already open) and writes both `auth_state.json` (Playwright `storage_state`, seeds Linux/Docker recovery) + `google_account.json` (cache for next wizard). Skip path is strong `y/N` with no default and an explicit consequence message. **Per session-158 audit discipline,** `GOOGLE_ACCOUNT_FILE` lives on `config.py` (not module-private) and is wired into `tests/test_path_resolution.py`'s allow-list + anti-drift scanner. **Tests:** `tests/test_wizard_signin.py` (11 cases) covers detection across present/absent/malformed artifacts + email regex; the live launch flow is unit-untested by design (Playwright mocking is brittle for persistent contexts) and gets its smoke test in Phase 14.8's clean-mac live-QA. ## Phase 15.8: CLI Verb Rename (`operator <name>` → `operator run <name>`)

*Disambiguate the agent invocation by requiring a directive verb. Bare `operator pm [url]` isn't action-oriented and collapses the "agents are brainchildren of the user" metaphor (reads as "operator, meet pm" — peer-to-peer introduction rather than directive). Directive verbs preserve the metaphor: `operator run pm` = "operator-system, run the operator named pm", same shape as `docker run nginx`. Chose `run` over `summon` / `send` / `meet` / `call` in session 149 — neutral developer vocabulary (matches `docker run`, `npm run`), platform-agnostic, keeps `try` / `setup` / `auth` reading as parallel verbs in the command table. Rejected dropping `operator` entirely: loose per-agent binaries (`pm`, `engineer`) would collide with generic shell vocabulary and fragment discoverability; OSS convention isn't "package name must lead" but "there must be one anchor users can grep shell history and docs for" — `operator <verb>` gives that anchor. **Sequenced before 14.5 `install.sh`** so the installer's "what's next" message, the README quickstart, and the wizard reveal all ship with the new form in one pass instead of a follow-up doc sweep.*


| Step   | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Status | Est. |
| ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | ---- |
| 15.8.0 | Audit — inventory every user-facing surface that echoes the bare `operator <name>` form, so the 15.8.1 rename lands atomically. Surfaces to walk: (a) `src/_1_800_operator/__main__.py` dispatcher, module docstring, `_print_usage`, and the "Restart with:" `ui.say` lines in `_run_macos` / `_run_linux`; (b) tests that hard-code the CLI shape — `tests/test_entry_cli.py` plus any wizard/setup tests that echo a launch command; (c) `README.md`, `src/_1_800_operator/agents/README.md`, `CLAUDE.md` (quick-start block + Commands section); (d) wizard reveal / success copy in `pipeline/setup.py` and any `ui.say` strings in `pipeline/ui.py`; (e) log / warning strings that suggest a command (Linux-adapter `A meeting URL is required on Linux:` help block; future install.sh stub references); (f) `docs/mvp-bar.md`, `docs/roadmap.md`, `docs/agent-context.md` example commands; (g) docstring references (e.g. `config.py`'s `OPERATOR_BOT` error pointing at `operator <name> [url]`). Output: short checklist captured in the 15.8.1 commit message so reviewers can verify nothing slipped.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | ✅      | ~30m |
| 15.8.1 | Rename — apply the audited changes atomically per the 15.8.0 inventory below. Dispatcher: `operator run <name> [url]` becomes the canonical form; bare `operator <name>` hard-fails with exit 2 + hint pointing at `operator run <name>` (no dual-accept — cleaner failure mode; avoids a transition period where two forms work and muddy support/telemetry). `try` / `setup` / `auth` / no-arg unchanged (already verbs / already print help). **Shipped session 150.** 21 documented changes landed across the 7 audited files; audit had missed 2 test cases in `test_entry_cli.py` (`test_main_known_bot_dispatches_to_run_bot` + `test_main_unknown_bot_returns_2` both exercised the bare form), so the commit also renames the first to `test_main_run_known_bot_dispatches_to_run_bot` and adds 3 new tests — `test_main_bare_known_bot_rejected_with_run_hint`, `test_main_run_without_name_returns_2`, `test_main_run_unknown_bot_returns_2`. `_print_usage` collapses the two-form lines into one `operator run <name> [url]` line with "auto-opens one if no url" inline. Dispatcher adds a `run` branch (with its own "unknown bot" branch pointing at usage) and a bare-known-bot branch that prints a pointed hint (`Run agents via \`operator run pm. Bare operator pm is no longer supported.`) + exits 2 — distinguishes known-but-bare from truly-unknown so the transition is self-documenting. 26/26` test_entry_cli.py`pass,`test_setup.py`pass,`python -m _1_800_operator pm`verified emitting the new hint and`python -m _1_800_operator` verified emitting the updated usage. | ✅      | ~1h  |

**Phase total: ~1.5h — shipped session 150 (15.8.0 audit-in-docs + 15.8.1 atomic rename).**

## Phase 15.9: `claude` Bundled Agent (Claude Code in your meeting)

*Fourth bundled agent whose defining trait is "auto-inherit the user's existing Claude Code setup." Positioning: target the Claude Code power-user audience with an agent that Just Works against their configured MCPs + skills. Hard-dependency on Claude Code being installed + logged in — the agent identity collapses without it. Sequenced before 14.5 `install.sh` so the installer ships a complete bundled roster of four. Non-blocking alongside 15.7.5/6 but a launch-quality bet: gives us a second launch moment ("Claude Code users get a first-class meeting agent").*


| Step   | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Status | Est.  |
| ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | ----- |
| 15.9.0 | Agent scaffold — `src/_1_800_operator/agents/claude/` with `config.yaml` + empty `skills/` placeholder. Agent block: `name=Claude`, `trigger_phrase=@claude`, tagline "Claude Code, in your meeting — plan-first, sandboxed, ready to delegate", captions off by default (chat-directed delegation, not ambient transcript listening). `claude-code` MCP enabled with beefed-up description calling out "built by Operator — sandboxed git worktree, nothing lands in your working tree until you approve" + `tool_timeout_seconds: 600`. All 9 other bundled MCPs present but `enabled: false` — wizard/first-run auto-import flips them on based on user's Claude Code config. Ground_rules: plan-first disposition + delegation rules inherited from engineer. | 15.9.1 | `_ensure_user_agents` sync-on-every-run — change the first-run seeding behavior from "copy bundled only if user dir is empty" to "copy any bundled bot missing from user dir." Lets new bundled agents (like `claude`) reach existing users without forcing them to delete `~/.operator/agents/`. Tradeoff: a user who deliberately deletes a bundled bot sees it reappear on next run — delete again. Smoke-tested against a fake-home fixture with existing `pm` — confirms all four bundled land including new `claude`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | ✅      | ~10m  |
| 15.9.2 | `pipeline/claude_code_import.py` — auto-discovery helpers. Three discovery sources: (a) `~/.claude.json` top-level `mcpServers` (locally-configured stdio and HTTP/SSE), (b) `claude mcp list` subprocess output (the authoritative source for claude.ai-hosted connectors like Gmail/Drive/Linear that don't live in any local file — regex-parsed, 10s timeout, degrades to empty on format drift or non-zero exit), (c) `~/.claude/skills/` and `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`. Transport classifier: stdio passthrough, HTTP/SSE auto-wrapped via `mcp-remote@0.1.38` (same pinned version as bundled Linear/Sentry) with `auth: oauth` + `auth_url` so the existing 15.7.3 cache-path check and `operator auth <name>` flow work unchanged on imports. Public `claude_code_installed_and_logged_in()` wraps `readiness._probe_claude_code(check_auth=True)`. `append_env_placeholders` appends `# VAR=` lines idempotently (checks both set and placeheld vars). 32 unit tests in `tests/test_claude_code_import.py` cover classify/slugify/read/extract/discover-CLI/discover-all/skills/CLAUDE.md/env-append + edge cases (missing file, malformed JSON, subprocess errors, trailing-newline handling). | ✅      | ~1.5h |
| 15.9.3 | Wizard hook — four surgical edits to `pipeline/setup.py`: (a) step 1 picker blocks selection of `claude` preset when Claude Code not installed/logged in (prints hint + recurses back to gallery — "option b" from the plan); (b) `_edit_preset("claude")` invokes new `_auto_import_claude_setup(state)` which calls `discover_all_mcps()`, merges imported MCPs into `state.bot_cfg["mcp_servers"]` (dedup by name — user curation wins), pre-populates `state.user_sources` with `~/.claude/skills/` dirs, stashes CLAUDE.md on state for step 4; (c) step 2 end: if `based_on == "claude"`, collect env-var refs from newly-enabled imports and call `append_env_placeholders` against `.env`; (d) step 3 top: surface auto-imported skills summary; (e) step 4: offer inline "Append ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md to ground rules? [y/N]" when the file exists. Smoke: `_edit_preset("claude")` against live Claude Code setup discovers 4 hosted MCPs (Gmail/Drive/Calendar/Linear) + 2 user skills correctly.                                                                                                                                                                                           | ✅      | ~1h   |
| 15.9.4 | CLI first-run hard-fail + auto-import — two hooks in `__main__.py::_run_bot`. (a) Hard-fail gate: when agent name is `claude`, run `claude_code_installed_and_logged_in()` before any config loads; on failure, print a clear stderr block pointing at claude.ai/code + `claude login` and exit 2. (b) `_bootstrap_claude_imports()` helper: idempotent first-run import via a `_claude_import_done: true` marker in the agent's `config.yaml`. First run loads config, calls `discover_all_mcps()`, merges new entries, appends env-var placeholders to `~/.operator/.env`, writes config back (PyYAML round-trip — comments lost on first write, matches wizard's existing behavior), sets marker. Subsequent runs skip entirely — keeps the ~3s `claude mcp list` shell-out off the hot path. Smoke: end-to-end against throwaway home (10 MCPs → 14 after, marker set, second call no-op); hard-fail mock test confirms exit 2 + clean stderr. Regression: 80+ tests green across 4 adjacent suites (test_claude_code_import, test_1574_readiness, test_chat_hardening, test_mcp_client).                                                                                                         | ✅      | ~45m  |
| 15.9.5 | Docs sync — roadmap (this block), `docs/deferred-live-tests.md` (4 new smoke entries: wizard-preset live pick, CLI first-run with real `~/.claude.json`, hard-fail path on a machine with `claude` CLI uninstalled, `claude mcp list` format-drift canary), `docs/handoff.md` session note, `CLAUDE.md` bundled-agent list mention.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | ✅      | ~20m  |


**Phase total: ~4h — shipped session TBD.**

**Key implementation finding.** `claude mcp list` is the authoritative source for claude.ai-hosted connectors (Gmail, Drive, Calendar, Linear — the MCPs most Claude Code power users actually have). `~/.claude.json#mcpServers` was the obvious candidate but is empty for users who configure MCPs via claude.ai account connectors rather than manual JSON edits. Parsing the CLI text output (10s timeout, non-match skip, degrades to empty) is the only way to surface these. All discovered hosted MCPs auto-wrap via `mcp-remote@0.1.38` with `auth: oauth`, so the existing 15.7.3 OAuth cache-path check and `operator auth <name>` flow catch them for free — no new auth code.

**Rejected scope.** Five translated slash-command skills (plan, meeting-recap, security-review, file-bug, code-cleanup) — session-151 audit inventoried them but user deferred post-launch per "ship the agent, skills later." Hosted-MCP CLI parse has a known brittleness axis: if Claude Code changes `claude mcp list` output format, discovery silently returns zero results and the import module degrades to `~/.claude.json` only. Monitor in Phase 17 upstream-drift watch.

## Phase 14.12: Two-Track Architecture Pivot ← BLOCKS LAUNCH

*Strategic pivot decided session 164 (Apr 25, late). Triggered by API-bill diagnosis: operator's `~/.operator/.env` ANTHROPIC_API_KEY was being inherited by spawned MCP server subprocesses (via `pipeline/mcp_client.py:593` `env={**os.environ, ...}`), and from there into the inner `claude -p --worktree` process. Inner claude CLI prefers env-var auth over claude.ai login when both are present, so every `delegate_to_claude_code` call was billing API rates rather than consuming the user's Claude Max subscription. A handful of delegates ate $3+ of API spend in a morning. Confirmed by `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl` showing `apiKeySource: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `model: claude-sonnet-4-6`.*

*The realization: the user has Claude Code working perfectly for solo work via Max subscription (free, generous, fast). Operator today forces them through an unrelated API-key path even when they don't need to — a worse experience that costs more. **Reframing: the "claude" bot's product value is "Claude Code in your meeting," and the cleanest way to deliver that is to actually use the user's Claude Code.** Permission MCP is the hosting capability Anthropic built specifically for cases like ours (a non-TTY caller wanting to gate inner-claude tool-use confirmations). The bot becomes a Meet front-end for Claude Code, not a re-implementation of half its features.*

***Two-track architecture:***

- ***Track A — `operator run claude*` (plug-and-play default)**. Zero setup, zero API key, zero customization. Inner LLM is `claude -p` subprocess (subscription-billed via user's Max plan). Permission MCP routes inner-claude tool confirmations through Meet chat. Personality + ground_rules pass through as system-prompt augmentation so the bot has meeting-tone voice (warm, brief, no walls of text) instead of solo-CLI voice. **The "claude" name is reserved exclusively for track A — wizard no longer offers it as a choosable preset.** Bundled operator MCPs (linear/github/sentry) are dropped from the claude bot since the user's claude.ai-connected MCPs cover the same surface and were already imported via Phase 15.9's `claude_code_import.py`. Bundled operator skills (codebase-walkthrough, migration-plan, etc.) ship as Claude Code skills in `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` on first run, so they're available to inner-claude natively (already designed as Claude Code skills).*
- ***Track B — `operator build*` (custom agent framework)**. Existing operator orchestration stays. Wizard pivots to "build a custom bot" only — user names it themselves, picks a provider (Anthropic API / OpenAI / local model via Ollama), wires their own MCPs, sets personality/ground_rules. All the configurability we've already built finds its natural home here. Power-user path with bring-your-own-keys billing.*

*The README's "Claude Code in your Google Meet" hero pitch becomes literal for track A; track B is the secondary "build your own meeting agent" story. Two paths, neither with billing surprises: track A is free for Max subscribers, track B is bring-your-own-keys.*

***Launch on hold.** User explicitly rejected the surgical "stop the bleeding" env-strip patch for current behavior. Direction: pivot fully now, regardless of launch timing. All Phase 14.5 / 14.8 / 16.x work pauses until 14.12 ships.*

                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Status | Est.                |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | ------------------- |
| 14.12.1 | **Permission MCP spike — does `claude -p` expose a host-resolvable permission callback for non-TTY callers?** Probe whether operator can register itself as a permission resolver so inner-claude's `tool_use` requests come back to us (chat-routable) instead of stalling on a TTY prompt or auto-bypassing. **Shipped session 165** — full report at `docs/permission-mcp-spike.md`, probes at `debug/permission_mcp_spike/`. Three probes ran end-to-end against `claude -p` under user's Claude Max subscription (no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`): probe 1 (happy path) confirmed PreToolUse hook + named-pipe IPC works, `apiKeySource: "none"` end-to-end; probe 2b confirmed sub-agent (Task tool) inner tool calls do NOT fire our hook (top-level dispatch DOES, with full sub-agent prompt visible) — opacity contained via worktree sandbox; probe 3 confirmed deny semantics (claude exits 0 with `permission_denials` populated, deny-reason text relayed back verbatim, no retries). Two corrections to early research: `--permission-prompt-tool` does NOT exist on the CLI (PreToolUse hook is the real mechanism); `--settings <file-or-json>` DOES exist despite docs (per-invocation registration path). SDK pathway researched but not probed — definitively API-key-only per [GitHub #559](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-agent-sdk-python/issues/559), structurally incompatible with track A's no-API-key promise. PreToolUse policy layering decided: 3 layers, no overlap — operator's hook itself is internal plumbing (not user-tunable), user's `~/.claude/settings.json` permission rules compose naturally via Claude Code's settings hierarchy, operator's "what to confirm in chat" knob exposed in track A config as `permissions.auto_approve` / `always_ask` lists. Stream-json events parsed for paragraph-flush parity with the Anthropic SDK path. System-prompt augmentation: operator passes personality + ground_rules via `--append-system-prompt` so claude's default system prompt and skills loading are preserved. **Removed from claude bot config:** bundled MCP servers (claude inherits from `~/.claude.json`), custom skills (claude loads `~/.claude/skills/` natively). Permission MCP wiring built (`pipeline/permission_bridge.py` + `pipeline/permission_chat_handler.py`) — PreToolUse hook fires synchronously, named-pipe IPC, chat round-trip resolves the decision. Worktree isolation dropped per session-166 redesign — chat-confirmation hook is the safety net, sub-agent opacity handled by denying the `Task` tool in `always_ask`. Restart-on-death implemented with probe 7's synthesized-opener strategy (bounded recovery latency, doesn't scale with meeting length). Subscription-auth assertion at startup (apiKeySource == "none") fail-loud if an API key leaks in. agents/claude/config.yaml rewritten 398→95 lines for track-A schema. Tests: 16 unit/smoke tests passing. **Shipped session 166 (`28153b9`); live-meeting Session 0 validation passed in session 167 (`6f6d7f3`); Sessions 1+2 PASS in session 168 (`0c1bcc9`, PR #5).** Session 167: 6 safety gates green + 6 bugs fixed; cold-start join 35s→12s. The original 14.12.4 plan (one-shot copy into the user's Claude Code skills dir) would cross the boundary by injecting operator's playbooks into the user's Claude Code env.
